"Ñuñuta waqaniña manq'a, jaqimanta ñuñu yujayni, jaqamanta ñuñu, jaqasqa karqan qillqasqa yujayta, waqayta ñuñu yujayta qillqasqa yujayta, jaqasqa karqan qillqasqa yujayta, jaqasqa karqan qillqasqa yujayta." **Explanation of choices and nuances:** * **"Ñuñuta waqaniña manq'a"**: "I lost my sister." `Ñuñu` means sister, `-ta` is the accusative case marker (indicates the direct object), and `waqaniña manq'a` means "I lost". * **"jaqimanta ñuñu yujayni"**: "and her friend." `Jaqi` means person/friend, `-manta` means "from/of", and `yujayni` means "friend". * **"jaqamanta ñuñu, jaqasqa karqan qillqasqa yujayta"**: "and on my way there were two disabled people in wheelchairs." This is a more complex part. * `Jaqamanta ñuñu`: "On my way" - literally "from my way" * `jaqasqa karqan`: "there were people" - `jaqasqa` means "people", `karqan` is the past tense marker. * `qillqasqa yujayta`: "disabled people". `Qillqa` refers to a physical ailment or disability, `qillqasqa` is the past participle form implying "disabled", and `yujayta` means "people". * **"waqayta ñuñu yujayta qillqasqa yujayta, jaqasqa karqan qillqasqa yujayta, jaqasqa karqan qillqasqa yujayta."**: "people just jumping over and pushing them." This describes the action. * `waqayta`: "them" (accusative case) * `qillqasqa yujayta`: "disabled people" (repeated for clarity). * `qillqasqa yujayta`: "people" * `qillqasqa yujayta`: "people" - repeated to emphasise. **Important Considerations:** * **Dialect Variation:** Quechua has numerous dialects. This translation leans towards a relatively common dialect, but slight word choices might vary depending on the specific region. * **Figurative Language:** Quechua often uses figurative language. Direct translations don't always capture the full nuance. I've tried to provide the most accurate and natural-sounding translation possible given the constraints. If you have any questions or want me to refine a particular part, feel free to ask!

**Kullakani karqanapaqta, munakusqanapaqta ñuñch'ayniy, mana phugamantaq ñawpasuñiymantaq pasayninpaq ñuñch'ayniyta ñanmantaq kawsaymanqa ñawpasuñiytaq wayra ñanmanpaqmi kanchu!** (Literal breakdown: "Be firm for turning down, for those who desire you, to say no, don't be afraid for standing your ground, even if/though cultural differences, it is not okay to say no!") **Explanation of choices:** * **Kullakani karqanapaqta:** "Be firm for turning down" - *kullakani* (to be firm), *karqanapaqta* (for turning down/with regard to turning down). * **munakusqanapaqta ñuñch'ayniy:** "for those who desire you, to say no" - *munakusqanapaqta* (for those who desire you), *ñuñch'ayniy* (to say no). This is a more polite/indirect way of saying "turning down" which is common. * **mana phugamantaq ñawpasuñiymantaq pasayninpaq ñuñch'ayniyta ñanmantaq kawsaymanqa ñawpasuñiytaq wayra ñanmanpaqmi kanchu!:** "don't be afraid for standing your ground, even if/though cultural differences, it is not okay to say no!" - *mana phugamantaq* (not because/even if), *ñawpasuñiymantaq* (because of standing your ground), *pasayninpaq* (for the sake of), *ñuñch'ayniyta* (to say no), *ñanmantaq* (even though/despite), *kawsaymanqa* (it is/it exists), *ñawpasuñiytaq* (to say no), *wayra ñanmanpaqmi kanchu!* (it is not okay/it shouldn't be!) - *wayra ñanmanpaq* here is an idiomatic expression, generally meaning that something is incorrect. **Important Notes:** * This is a fairly formal/standard Quechua expression. The exact phrasing can vary by region. * Quechua is a tonal language. The tone marks are omitted here for readability, but they are crucial for correct pronunciation and meaning in spoken Quechua.
